  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4002eac2-a387-4bee-b505-c67b048e6922'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_226365267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/226365267" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/226365267?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=didn-t-finish">didn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer226365267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12091735636368962936">OH - GOOD - GRIEF.<br/><br/>That's all I can say here. I started out with an open mind, I was looking forward to this book, I like action adventure and I'll forgive a lot if the book has a good action feel. Also, I'm a fantasy fan so I'm practiced at "suspending disbelief", I'll swallow a lot with a shrug and an "oh well" if it makes a good story.<br/><br/>This time...it didn't.<br/><br/>I've never read anything by Mr. Reilly before. Here he seems to have taken a page from Bullwinkle J. Moose's book. He combined Peabody's Im</span>
  <span id="freeText12091735636368962936" style="display:none">OH - GOOD - GRIEF.<br /><br />That's all I can say here. I started out with an open mind, I was looking forward to this book, I like action adventure and I'll forgive a lot if the book has a good action feel. Also, I'm a fantasy fan so I'm practiced at "suspending disbelief", I'll swallow a lot with a shrug and an "oh well" if it makes a good story.<br /><br />This time...it didn't.<br /><br />I've never read anything by Mr. Reilly before. Here he seems to have taken a page from Bullwinkle J. Moose's book. He combined Peabody's Improbable History and Fractured Fairy Tales and got some seriously fractured history. Interestingly if this had been the only problem, I think (again) I could have shrugged it off and gone on, but it was just "one bridge too far". <br /><br />Most of the reasons this book ended on the "discard" pile I'll put under a spoiler warning, but a couple of things show up as the book opens. The book begins with a "portentous" opening concerning the Seven Wonders of the Ancient World, primarily the capstone of the Great Pyramid. From there we launch into the book with what is obviously an expedition to obtain <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ a part of the capstone of the Great Pyramid <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. The first "huh" moment is quick in coming. These tough, seasoned, experienced adventurers have brought along as a member of their crew...a little girl. You see there's something she can do and they "couldn't come up with any way to handle it", that didn't involve bringing a little girl into a "place" rife with death traps, crocodiles and other humans who will stop at nothing to get to "the item" before them...killers. Okay, right. I had a "bad movie flashback moment" there. I flashed on the Schwarzenegger movie, Last Action Hero, in which a "kid" keeps trying to convince the "action hero" that they're really in a movie. When the police captain assigns the boy to the cop as a "punishment" the "kid" (Austin O'Brien) shouts that in "real life" they'd never assign a kid as his partner they'd call Social Services. It doesn't make a dent. Same here.<br /><br />Okay we brought a small child into deadly danger, cool. I'll grin and move on.<br /><br />Next we get the silly. Since we have a little girl on the team, we can't have nasty threatening call or code names for the other team members, no they're called things like Big Ears and Pooh Bear... <br /><br />Okay, again I could live with it, but things went from bad to worse. From here I go under a spoiler warning. So, bottom line for you who don't want a spoiler, I hope you like it better than me. I was disappointed and finally put it aside as I have a lot of books waiting to be read and this isn't one I want to put my time into nor can I recommend it.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Okay, just us now. <br /><br />From the above let us proceed. Getting through the "death traps" is fairly straight forward as their "team genius" has been able to study and find the keys to getting through (of course only a couple of children in all the world can read the language of Thoth, so they always have to get the little girl with them to the front when something has to be read, like which key hole won't kill them). Okay, we get through the traps...mostly unscathed. Yeah, we lost one guy, but he showed back up later un-crushed by the huge stone that had been set to kill as an intricate and sly deathtrap. Whew, good thing it didn't work even though they set it off. Well, it worked but they guy survived the death trap...some how...oh well.<br /><br />Then we "meet" one of the two (other) groups who are competing for the capstone.<br /><br />You see if "we" (that is humanity) don't set the capstone back on the pyramid within 7 days a sunspot will cause horrible weather, floods etc. and destroy the entire world...or at least civilization. (It would be like if they hadn't made people realize how BAD it is to drive SUVs, smoke [in public], use incandescent light-bulbs, eat Whopper Burgers, candy bars, drink sugared soft drinks or for that matter if they can't outlaw Big-Gulps and other drinks over sixteen ounces.) Our heroes (of course) want to replace the stone for "noble reasons" the other two groups (basically the Freemasons and the Catholic Church) want to save the world for "selfish nefarious" reasons (You know like THRUSH in the man from U.N.C.L.E. or KAOS from <i>Get Smart</i> who wanted to destroy the world for personal gain [don't ask me I didn't write it]).<br /><br />Anyway, the bad guys have guns. (Isn't everyone who has a gun a bad guy? It seems so here at times)(This by the way gives me pause because I'm not only a shooter but have a goatee [or possibly a Van Dyke, I have a mustache and I'm never sure which one has a mustache and which one doesn't]. Based on my gun ownership I may be a bad guy. Based on my facial hair and Star Trek I may be the evil twin of someone in an alternate universe somewhere?)Anyway, back to the guns... LUCKILY, our resident genius once designed a special "bullet like object" (it can't be an actual type of <i>bullet</i> itself as he [being a <i>good</i> guy would never invent a bullet)that can be fired (don't ask me, again. I would assume it's fired from a gun but that seems so...you know unlikely) and it sets up a sort of magnetic field that causes all "bullets" to go haywire and just fall down. For some reason this apparently works on ALL bullets (or almost all as we'll see in a second), even those with copper jackets and those that are totally unjacketed lead projectiles (even though copper and lead are nonmagnetic). I mean I can see it effecting bullets jacketed and half jacked in steel...but lead? Later one of the "good guys" shoots someone with a rubber bullet (of course, what other kind would a good guy have?) and that bullet works fine...okay, fine I could live with it, again.<br /><br />We find in the course of the book that a large part of the US Military are now subverted by the Freemasons, so one group of bad guys is largely "basically" made up of American Military. (Our genius sold his magic magnetic bullet stopper to the U.S. Military some years before this...but they broke it and can't make it work). The main assumption here seems to me to be that the U.S. Military is made up almost entirely of idiots and psychopaths. (We meet one of the psychopaths as we're escaping...see West knew him, before he [that is west] became a good guy apparently.)(Another thought...can you be an idiot AND a psychopath?) <br /><br />The other Bad Guy Group are Europeans. They are "basically" (again) the Catholic Church...I'm not sure if it's the same bunch that was after Robert Langdon however. Maybe you can watch for that?????? You know...let me know if you find out.<br /><br />WE also find out (from our resident genius) that Alexander the Great and Ptolemy are apparently at least in some sense responsible for the construction of all the seven ancient wonders (and hiding the seven pieces of the capstone you see). See, Alexander was the last person to have the stone. He broke it up, so no one could have all that power. Good ol' Alexander. What a guy, huh?<br /><br />By the time I got through all this I was turning the tolerance filter up, up and up again on my suspension of disbelief-o-meter (or is that suspension of "belief", oh well [again][I seem to be saying "oh well" a lot])...but when we also find that many organizations including the Knights of Saint John and much of the Catholic Church are nothing more than continuations of the Cult of Amun-Ra...well somewhere in here my <b>crap</b> filter completely failed and the solid-waste-o-meter red-lined.... I'm sorry, I have a limited amount of time on this earth and there are a lot of books I want to fit into that time. This one gets put aside, discarded, pitched, thrown away.... <br /><br />In other words I stopped and put it aside unfinished. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So as noted if it's your cup of tea, enjoy, I'm happy for you. Again really, I mean it, enjoy. To each their own. There's no accounting for taste AND any and all other cliches that are applicable. I'll just move on. Thank you.... <br /><br />Allow me to add a quote attributed Dorthy Parker which I've used before:<br /><br /><b> <i>"This is not a novel to be tossed aside lightly. <br />It should be thrown with great force."</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12091735636368962936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1678820144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1678820144" />
    <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans"><img alt="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587115780p2/7298986.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1678820144?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)" href="/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans">✘✘ Sarah ✘✘ (former Nefarious Breeder of Murderous Crustaceans)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/25618612-seven-ancient-wonders">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=grammar-committed-suicide">grammar-committed-suicide</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=crappity-crap">crappity-crap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=my-friends-corrupted-my-soul">my-friends-corrupted-my-soul</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=boredom-fest">boredom-fest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=tbr-shelf-says-thank-you">tbr-shelf-says-thank-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=lame-a-saurus">lame-a-saurus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-suspense">mysteries-thrillers-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans?shelf=me-not-write-good-english">me-not-write-good-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1678820144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15820067290811622492"><b>To the person who wrote</b> this <s>PoC™</s> slightly not very good story: who the fish are you, and what have you done with the guy who wrote <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/144790.Ice_Station?from_search=true&search_version=service' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ice Station</a>?! <b>You cannot be Matthew Reilly</b>. That is just impossible. Because, seriously, this book here? It feels like it was written 30 years ago. By my 13-year-old niece. Who doesn't speak a word of English. Yep, that's right. <b>This ain't no Pulitzer prize material, my Little Barnacles</b>.<br/><br/><b>Wait</b>. Before I roll out my <b>Deadly Arguments of Mass Book Destruction</b> (DAoMBD™), </span>
  <span id="freeText15820067290811622492" style="display:none"><b>To the person who wrote</b> this <s>PoC™</s> slightly not very good story: who the fish are you, and what have you done with the guy who wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/144790.Ice_Station?from_search=true&amp;search_version=service" rel="nofollow noopener">Ice Station</a>?! <b>You cannot be Matthew Reilly</b>. That is just impossible. Because, seriously, this book here? It feels like it was written 30 years ago. By my 13-year-old niece. Who doesn't speak a word of English. Yep, that's right. <b>This ain't no Pulitzer prize material, my Little Barnacles</b>.<br><br><b>Wait</b>. Before I roll out my <b>Deadly Arguments of Mass Book Destruction</b> (DAoMBD™), I have a message for the lovely person who was <b>hilarious</b> enough to suggest I read this book: my dear <s>Trish</s> anonymous friend, I love you, but send me another rec similar to this one and you're <b>dead meat</b>. Then again, you might not like me a great deal after reading my DAoMBD™, so I guess I shouldn't worry too much about you contacting me. Ever. Again. Oh well. <b>It was nice knowing you, anyway</b>! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467410109i/19590195.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Soooooo. Where were we?</b> Oh yes, I-can't-believe-you're-Matthew-Reilly's high-quality writing. Such awesomeness there. It's bloody brilliant. I love it. Which <b>loosely</b> translates to mean: it's outdated. It's simplistic. It's repetitive. <s>It's crappy</s>. It's OTT. It's an <b>insult to the Grammar Gods</b>. It's slightly (if only a little bit) subpar. Kind of. Somewhat. And it makes me wonder if anyone bothered to <b>edit the freaking book</b>. I mean, what editor in their right mind would let an author get away with such a <b>deadly onslaught of exclamation points</b>? I'm telling you, my Little Barnacles, this is the stuff of legend. I'm a pretty open-minded girl (sometimes) and I've never had anything against these poor, innocent punctuation marks, but there is only so much <b>forced excitement</b> the little heart I don't have can take. And no matter how super uber tough and nefarious I am, I could <b>barely survive</b> some of the paragraphs in this book. I kid you not. Don't believe me? Very well. Read this and <b>try not to choke</b> (this is not for the faint of heart, people, so I'll use spoiler tags to spare the feeble and the weak):<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>‘Pooh Bear<b>!</b> Get out of here<b>!</b>’ West called. ‘What about you<b>!</b>’ Pooh yelled back. West nodded back down his aqueduct tunnel. ‘No other option<b>!</b> I have to go this way<b>!</b>’ ‘Jack<b>!</b>’ Wizard called. ‘What<b>!</b>’ ‘Judah used a tunnel-boring vehicle to drill through the old filled-in excavation tunnel<b>!</b> They must be planning to take the Pieces out that way<b>!</b> Check your sketch<b>!</b> You may still be able to get a look at the Pieces<b>!</b> All may not be lost<b>!</b>’ ‘I’ll do my best<b>!</b>’ West nodded at the expanding mud pool. ‘Now get out of here<b>!</b> Call Sky Monster<b>!</b> Get to the Halicarnassus<b>!</b> I’ll catch up somehow<b>!</b>’</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Multiply this</b> ↑↑↑ by the 544 pages in this book and you get <b>mass punctuation-induced suicides</b>. So tragic.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467405647i/19589667.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Please</b>, person-who-is-supposed-to-be-Matthew-Reilly, listen to Marky Mark here, the guy knows his stuff. It's high time for you to stop <b>mistreating exclamation marks</b> in such a shameful way. What did they ever do to you, anyway? <b>And what about these poor italics</b>? Did you really need to brutalize them like that? AND don't get me started about the <b>italicized interjections with built-in exclamation points</b> *shakes head in utter desperation*<br><br><i>Whoosh<b>!</b></i><br><i>Whap<b>!</b></i><br><i>Boom<b>!</b></i><br><i>Ahhhh<b>!</b></i><br><i>Zing-smack<b>!</b></i> (my personal favourite)<br><i>Whump<b>!</b></i><br><br><b>Such clever, resourceful writing</b>. Come to think of it, reading this book kind of feels like reading a <s>bad</s> comic. Without the graphics. And that's pretty cool, if you ask me ← <i>this might or might not be a slightly sarcastic comment on my part. And I may or may not have felt like this while reading this book:</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467411709i/19590336.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>I ain't naught but a crappy, harebrained reviewer</b>. Yes, I am sadly aware of that very unfortunate fact. And yet, I shall be so bold as to give you a <s>friendly</s> piece of crustacean advice, person-who-is-supposed-to-be-Matthew-Reilly: <b>your readers are not stupid</b> (well most of them, anyway). You DO NOT need to use freaking exclamation marks and freaking italics every two freaking seconds to make sure they get <b>how they are supposed to feel</b>. They might be nothing more than lowly barnacles, but they have one or two grey cells, and they WILL eventually get the point <b>all by their little selves</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467407144i/19589801.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>So</b>. Now that I've brilliantly established how <b>delightfully written</b> this book is, let me tell you about the <b>fascinating story</b> itself. Wait. Have I already told how fascinating this story is? I have? Oops, sorry about that. It's just that the <b>exquisitely intricate plot</b> made such a big impression on me that I need to rehash a bit to make sure you realize <b>how awesome</b> it was. I could use exclamation marks to get my point across, too<b>!</b> But I'm not like that<b>!</b> Oh no<b>!</b> Not me<b>!</b> You're so lucky, my Little Barnacles<b>!</b> <b>No OD'ing on punctuation today!</b><br><br><b>But I digress</b>. This book? Let's see…Take the <b>worst Indiana Jones rip-offs</b> you've ever seen/read/whatever, throw in a bunch of <b>slightly clichéd and a tinsy bit stereotyped military types</b>, make them go through the very same quests/trials/adventures <b>every other chapter</b> (same shit, different location. It's all delightfully refreshing), add a dash of <b>never-before-seen-and-oh-so-suspenseful</b> scenes (think ceiling-coming-down-on-the-good-guys, rolling boulder booby traps and the like), a bunch of <b>beautifully complex</b> ☢ <i>sarcasm alert</i> ☢ characters, and you get this gem of a captivating story. <b>It's all pretty glorious, if you ask me</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467409737ra/19590135.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>And now for the icing on the cake</b>! Presenting the one and only, the invincible, the <b>mostest awesomest</b> {cue drum roll} Jack West<b>!</b> He is pretty much <b>perfect!</b> He can do no wrong! He is <b>superiorly clever</b> (well not quite as Einsteinian as I am, but almost)<b>!</b> He has mysterious secrets<b>!</b> His all-encompassing knowledge about ancient stuff is <b>seriously all-encompassing!</b> And he <b>kicks major ass</b>, too! I'm telling you, my Little Barnacles, Superman and Spiderman combined are <b>useless, brainless wimps</b> compared to this guy. Damn. Why didn't I lock him up in my harem when I had the chance?! I should know a HOT, BADASS DUDE when I see one! I think I might be losing my legendary touch. <b>Double damn</b>.<br><br>➽ <b>And the moral of this Most of my Friends Loved this Book They Must Therefore Be Slightly Insane Review</b> (MomFLtBTMTBSIR™) is: death by exclamation point is horrific, slow and abominably painful. So stay away from the murderous punctuation marks, my Little Barnacles, <b>for they are treacherous and up to no good</b>.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15820067290811622492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4213258-bradley?shelf=2016-shelf">2016-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679094415" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16923147160728483592">I say it's SF, but that's only because I haven't bothered to add an Action/Adventure category.<br/><br/>For this is what it is! Yeah, robot arms and flying suits and all, but best of all, and adventure to pick up your 5000 year old Legos or Amon Ra is gonna smite you!<br/><br/>Say what? Is that even in this book? Well, sortof. <br/><br/>What we do have is a rollicking adventure that aims for the sort of pure WOW and AWE factor that is generally missing from today's literature, taking us on a tour through all the Seven Wonder</span>
  <span id="freeText16923147160728483592" style="display:none">I say it's SF, but that's only because I haven't bothered to add an Action/Adventure category.<br /><br />For this is what it is! Yeah, robot arms and flying suits and all, but best of all, and adventure to pick up your 5000 year old Legos or Amon Ra is gonna smite you!<br /><br />Say what? Is that even in this book? Well, sortof. <br /><br />What we do have is a rollicking adventure that aims for the sort of pure WOW and AWE factor that is generally missing from today's literature, taking us on a tour through all the Seven Wonders of the World, or whatever is left of them, and doing it without much care in the world for little things like logic. Who needs it?<br /><br />The book is BIG and Wild and Emotional and best of all, it's full of ancient traps. I'm not kidding. It almost overwhelms the page. As I read this I might as well have been watching Indiana Jones and the Temple of Doom on steroids. There's even a little kid. All these burly men in the midst of gun-porn have no problems laying their lives down for her. It's odd but it resolves itself because she's mystically special. <br /><br />Hell, the whole book is mystically special. :) Add heavy Dan Brown-ish conspiracy theories, wild ancient stories, the Giza Pyramid's capstone, and you'll have a wild feel like the original GI Joe cartoon when they were all on that mystical quest stuff.<br /><br />Don't get me wrong. I like a good and kooky comic book feel culminating with evil Masonic Americans and evil Catholic Amon Ra worshipers in Europe. I especially love being transported into great pacing, almost non-stop action, and never-ending tests of skill, capture, and pathos. It's kinda perfect for any action movie fan. :) Just turn off the brain and flow with it.<br /><br />This is the definition of popcorn fiction. And I thought that UF's had it going, lol. I swear I saw Chuck Norris in here.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16923147160728483592" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_43777136" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/43777136" />
    <a title="Tracy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1933201-tracy"><img alt="Tracy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232455953p2/1933201.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/43777136?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy" href="/user/show/1933201-tracy">Tracy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1933201-tracy?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1933201-tracy?shelf=donated">donated</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer43777136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3003781695887018309">This book was so completely terrible, so absolutely lacking in anything resembling worth, that I simply had to talk about it. It is so bad that I couldn't believe it, and kept reading with the sole purpose to find out how bad it could really get, and so I could tell everybody I knew how totally, completely, wholly bad it was. The only other books I have ever even started to read that were this bad were a few cheesy romance novels, and I wondered how even those could get published.<br/><br/>Where to begin?</span>
  <span id="freeText3003781695887018309" style="display:none">This book was so completely terrible, so absolutely lacking in anything resembling worth, that I simply had to talk about it. It is so bad that I couldn't believe it, and kept reading with the sole purpose to find out how bad it could really get, and so I could tell everybody I knew how totally, completely, wholly bad it was. The only other books I have ever even started to read that were this bad were a few cheesy romance novels, and I wondered how even those could get published.<br /><br />Where to begin? I suppose if I had to explain why this book was so amazingly awful in a few words, I could simply point out that the characters were flat, uninteresting stereotypes, the plot was a sad, lame attempt at copying an Indiana Jones movie smashed together with a Dan Brown novel, and the writing itself was so incompetent that a seventh grade teacher would be hard-pressed to give it a good grade.<br /><br />Then there's the fact that the motivations of characters and events are told to us with embarrassing clumsiness, major plot points are illogical to the point of absurdity (even beyond the suspension of disbelief you need for a story that revolves around the magical power of the Great Pyramid), and sweeping generalizations based on nationality are made at every turn, with the Evil Americans heading the pack.<br /><br />But there's so much more to the horrific tragedy that is this book!<br /><br />The plot is basically this: the missing top of the Great Pyramid of Giza has magical powers that will give one country on Earth supreme power if they put some dirt in it on a certain date. But of course, the missing pieces are missing, aren't they? They have been cleverly hidden in the seven wonders of the ancient world, to prevent some a-hole nation from gaining too much power. Guess which a-hole nation is trying to steal power a week before the special day? Also, if the missing pieces aren't put back on top of the Pyramid by noon on the special day, a big sunspot will melt everybody on the planet. Or something.<br /><br />The heros of our story are trying to stop all the bad stuff from happening, naturally. We're given an awkward alliance of nations that the rest of the world doesn't seem to think are important - Ireland, Canada, Spain, New Zealand, Israel (Israel? really?), Jamaica, the United Arab Emirates, and Australia. Oh, and there's a little girl, on whom everything rests. The bad guys are the Americans, who stomp around killing people, stealing things, and being uniformly evil, and the European Union, with an evil Italian priest, the little girl's evil twin, and a whole bunch of French guys who are also uniformly evil, if devoid of distinction.<br /><br />And that's about it for depth of story. Everything is cobbled together directly from Indiana Jones, with a healthy dose of Dan Brown conspiracy (complete with Freemason US Presidents and Catholic Church sun-worship) and the Australian version of Dirk Pitt from Clive Cussler's adventure novels. We're given a load of ancient wonders which have been hidden for millennia but which are easily found thanks to some ancient documents and scrolls. Each one has a load of "traps" which are always easily and quickly neutralized by our heroes, but which kill hordes of faceless bad guys. There's plenty of action all over the globe, from robbing the Louvre to cave-diving in Egypt to breaking into Guantanamo Bay to trekking across the Iraqi desert to murder on the plains of Kenya, but all of it takes place within a week and requires a private plane with unlimited fuel (stolen from Saddam Hussein) and a cheeky Kiwi pilot who apparently never needs to sleep.<br /><br />The characters are so poorly drawn that the soullessly wicked Americans aren't even the worst offense (although the main evil one is named Judah - come on!). A couple of chapters in to the book, convinced that Reilly must hate Americans with an unholy passion, I skipped to the Q &amp; A with the author at the back of the book, where he says that he doesn't hate Americans - heck, he's even met some and a few of them are actually quite intelligent! - but that he just needed a villain and they were so convenient. I then realized that Reilly is just totally incapable of characterization. Our main hero is presented as cool, detached, and lethal, but with a soft spot for the little girl - but this all has to be told to us (over and over) because the character's actions are completely inconsistent. The other characters have no distinction whatsoever, and are only delineated by goofy nicknames given to them by the little girl and by their adherence to the stereotypes of their given nationality.<br /><br />By far the worst insult to the intelligence of the reader, however, is the extremely atrocious writing. There is an excessive use of demonstrative punctuation: exclamation points, italics, random paragraph and sentence breaks, the hyphen trail-off followed by a combination of all of the above. There is the recurrent use of sound-effect words, too, so one is constantly left with the feeling that the author is trying to describe a movie he saw once, but is too drunk to command an adequate vocabulary.<br /><br />I could go on and on about how truly abysmal this book is (and yes, I did have to check the thesaurus for more ways to say "bad"), but really, I've already spent too much time on it already. Please, for the love of God, don't read this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3003781695887018309" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_39055402" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39055402" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39055402?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">high-octane A/A globe-trotting fiction fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-or-autobuy-author">favorite-or-autobuy-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=all-things-spring-challenge">all-things-spring-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-to-die-for">hero-to-die-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=2012-sky-s-the-limit-club">2012-sky-s-the-limit-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=ancient-history">ancient-history</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=dangerous-hero-2012-general-reading">dangerous-hero-2012-general-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=daddy-hero">daddy-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39055402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9579346720013590456">Seven Deadly Wonders introduces a new character by Matthew Reilly to me, Jack West Jr. It's very hard to follow in the footsteps of Shane 'Scarecrow' Schofield, because, well, he's the man! But I have to say I really do like Jack. What's not to like about him? He's a fun character. Honorable, intelligent, athletic, dedicated, daring, and lethal to the bad guys. And being a girl who grew up on Indiana Jones, and wanted to be her own version of the adventurer, Jack has an Indiana Jones in a modern</span>
  <span id="freeText9579346720013590456" style="display:none">Seven Deadly Wonders introduces a new character by Matthew Reilly to me, Jack West Jr. It's very hard to follow in the footsteps of Shane 'Scarecrow' Schofield, because, well, he's the man! But I have to say I really do like Jack. What's not to like about him? He's a fun character. Honorable, intelligent, athletic, dedicated, daring, and lethal to the bad guys. And being a girl who grew up on Indiana Jones, and wanted to be her own version of the adventurer, Jack has an Indiana Jones in a modern setting appeal. <br /><br />I thought this story was a clever idea. I had watched a documentary on The Seven Wonders of the Ancient World, and they inspired a great awe in this history buff. To read a story in which our intrepid heroes track down these wonders, not for selfish reasons, but to save the world, was both interesting and exciting. This is one of those books I could not read quietly, which makes me happy I wasn't trying to read it in mixed company. It is full of scenes where I gasped out loud regularly, verbally and under my breath yelled insults at the bad guys, cheered and laughed. This is the brilliance of Matt Reilly. He is one of those writers that engages you and gives you a fun read that takes you out of your regular world and into danger and adventure. It's not always without loss or risk, because sometimes you lose characters you grew fond of along the way. In the end though, I know that good will win out. If it didn't in these books, I wouldn't be a Matt Reilly fan anymore.<br /><br />I liked the found family that I met with Jack and his team. I am a tremendous sucker for a father figure hero. Even though Jack isn't the touchy-feely type, you can tell he loves young Lily like crazy, not as a mere means to an end or a mission. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I almost cried when she called him Daddy and it shocked him in a good way. Yes, I am a sap, which you probably know already!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I have to say, I liked that Reilly wasn't afraid to make the Americans the bad guys. In his Q&amp;A, he explained his reasonings and made it clear he has nothing against Americans. I wasn't mad at him anyway, but I tell you, I was hating on the bad guys something fierce. But honestly, he spread some of the bad guy yuck around evenly. <br /><br />Warning: If you are a Christian, don't take some of the stuff about the Catholic church and the so called origins of some of the tenets of the church (indirectly Christianity) seriously. Before I started getting annoyed, I just rolled my eyes. It's a fiction book, and I am not trying to take offense at that stuff, and I don't think Reilly was trying to criticize or devalue Christianity itself. He has bit of the Illuminati thing going on, but doesn't call them that. Suffice it so say, if you have any conspiracy theory leanings, you will appreciate some of the elements about secret societies in this book. <br /><br />The writing style isn't erudite or lofty. It's serviceable and casual. I just went with it, and I have to say that it fits the story. I like that Reilly writes fun books. He's not worried about being a member of the literary elite (which is fine with me because I hate book snobbery). At the same time, I felt like he worked hard to deliver a good quality read, and a lot of plotting went into this story. I appreciate the diagrams and illustrations, because I would have given myself an aneurysm trying to visualize a lot of it. <br /><br />If you have any ancient history geek leanings like myself, here is a writeup on <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seven_Wonders_of_the_Ancient_World" rel="nofollow noopener">the Seven Wonders of the Ancient World</a>. It's exciting stuff, if you're a nerd, anyway. <br /><br />As usual, there is some blood and violence. That's sort of Reilly's thing, but he doesn't focus as much on it in this book as in the others I read by him because this is more adventure than action. There are a lot thrills as they navigate dangerous ancient traps and pitfalls to get to the artifacts. Good stuff! I don't like gore much, I did the excitement of the over-the-top action scenes. Some parts had me laughing because they were so crazy!<br /><br /><b>Final Thoughts</b>:<br /><br />If you want a fun and educational in a 'doesn't take itself to seriously kind of way' read, with a lovable, larger than life (but rather humble) hero, and a great ensemble, with a cute but highly intelligent little girl thrown in, look no further! (Warning: Run on sentence!) If you like ancient history but want to have fun at the same time, this book is for you. If you watched Indiana Jones a lot and still haven't moved on, check out Seven Deadly Wonders!<br /><br />Overall rating: <b>4.5/5.0 stars</b><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9579346720013590456" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_901443176" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/901443176" />
    <a title="Krystal" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18989854-krystal"><img alt="Krystal" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491478087p2/18989854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/901443176?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystal" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystal" href="/user/show/18989854-krystal">Krystal</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781742611730" href="/book/show/17213977-seven-ancient-wonders">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=dymocks-101-club">dymocks-101-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=carnage-and-mayhem">carnage-and-mayhem</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=aussie-authors">aussie-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=motley-crew">motley-crew</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18989854-krystal?shelf=owned">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer901443176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4503908396680111797"><b>**Re-read 07/20**</b><br/><br/>Not gonna lie - Reilly's writing is completely <i>outrageous</i>.<br/><br/><b>I am 100% here for it.</b><br/><br/>It's so over-the-top and action-packed and full of miraculous moments and impressive saves and <b>I FKN LOVE EVERY MINUTE OF IT.</b><br/><br/>This book introduces us to one of my favourite fictional heroes: Jack West Jr. He's basically a badass blend of John McClane, Indiana Jones and Aragorn from <i>LOTR</i> - some of my faves right there - and he's accompanied by a hardcore team of warriors from around the globe as they r</span>
  <span id="freeText4503908396680111797" style="display:none"><b>**Re-read 07/20**</b><br /><br />Not gonna lie - Reilly's writing is completely <i>outrageous</i>.<br /><br /><b>I am 100% here for it.</b><br /><br />It's so over-the-top and action-packed and full of miraculous moments and impressive saves and <b>I FKN LOVE EVERY MINUTE OF IT.</b><br /><br />This book introduces us to one of my favourite fictional heroes: Jack West Jr. He's basically a badass blend of John McClane, Indiana Jones and Aragorn from <i>LOTR</i> - some of my faves right there - and he's accompanied by a hardcore team of warriors from around the globe as they race to find pieces of an ancient artefact that was long ago divided into seven parts and hidden in the seven ancient wonders of the world. Along for the ride is Lily - a vital piece of the puzzle, despite the fact that, apart from an uncanny gift for languages, she's a pretty normal ten-year-old.<br /><br /><b>It jumps straight into the action,</b> with the team racing against vicious opposing forces to conquer an ancient system of traps to recover the first segment. The traps are wonderfully creative throughout the entire novel - as are the solutions to overcoming them. This is pretty consistent throughout the series - always interesting puzzles to solve! Naturally, not everyone gets out alive ... and we get some nice graphic depictions of these deaths. I mean, what's the point in having a pit full of crocs if no one is going to fall in, right?!<br /><br /><b>I love the sheer madness of the adventure</b> and the creativity of the traps and deaths and the puzzles of the ancient wonders. I love the history that is integrated, and how <b>real, factual information has been twisted to fit the story</b> so neatly. I particularly love the <b>pictures and diagrams</b> that allow me to understand the locations and visualise everything so much better. <br /><br />Jack's team is also full of some <b>really lovable characters.</b> Reilly's writing style means none of them are safe, but that makes the risk-taking that much more exciting, and you really do pick your faves and hope they make it out okay. There are also some beautiful moments seeing these hardcore warriors reveal their softer sides in their dealings with young Lily, who is a very clever kid. There's a bird, too - speaking of clever.<br /><br />It's not particularly realistic by any means but it is <b>fast, fascinating, and action-packed.</b> There are no boring bits, and there are plenty of heroes and villains and violent deaths. There's a bit of mystery surrounding the puzzles of the pieces and the ancient history adds a depth to all the gung-ho that makes it a more intellectual offering perhaps than Reilly's other popular <i>Scarecrow</i> series.<br /><br />It's also a complete adventure on its own while still leaving plenty of desire for a sequel. (Lucky for us there are already five more, with the sixth book in the series coming out October this year and a promised 7th to conclude the series.)<br /><br />Honestly I love this series so it was so much fun to go back and re-read the story where it all began! Highly recommend for the action-lovers, the treasure-hunters and those who enjoy ancient history with a side of modern violence. How can you not want to read it with that plug, am I right?<br /><br /><br /><b>**Original review 08/15**</b><br /><br />Another brilliantly ridiculous, action-packed novel by Matthew Reilly. Firstly, if you enjoy realistic situations, forget it. There is far too much coincidence for anyone looking for realism. On the other hand, if you like fast and hard action with fascinating variety and an element of mystery, this delivers. Great collection of characters doing batsh*t insane things in crazy situations with very little reprieve. I really enjoyed the overall story of the ancient wonders, and I think it's this theme that makes me prefer this introductory novel to Ice Station. Can't wait to read the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4503908396680111797" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_131275294" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/131275294" />
    <a title="Lee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4369018-lee"><img alt="Lee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286124146p2/4369018.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/131275294?book_show_action=true">Nov 17, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lee" href="/user/show/4369018-lee">Lee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780330426572" href="/book/show/1282342.Seven_Ancient_Wonders">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4369018-lee?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer131275294" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1490413472493471419">A few weeks ago someone in my apartment building left a bunch of old magazines and recipe books in the lobby on a shelf that acts as a kind of internal charity shop. Amongst the 2008 editions of Marie Claire magazines was this book. Judging the book by its cover I assumed it would be god-awful pop fiction riding the Dan Brown bandwagon, so I of course picked it up and read it today on a return trip to Oxford.<br/><br/>I confess, the book isn't terrible. I'm used to suspending my sense of disbelief when re</span>
  <span id="freeText1490413472493471419" style="display:none">A few weeks ago someone in my apartment building left a bunch of old magazines and recipe books in the lobby on a shelf that acts as a kind of internal charity shop. Amongst the 2008 editions of Marie Claire magazines was this book. Judging the book by its cover I assumed it would be god-awful pop fiction riding the Dan Brown bandwagon, so I of course picked it up and read it today on a return trip to Oxford.<br /><br />I confess, the book isn't terrible. I'm used to suspending my sense of disbelief when reading, but I wasn't aware when I started it that Matthew Reilly books require the reader to completely disregard the physical rules of our universe, maybe if I'd been forewarned I'd have enjoyed the book more. But like I said: it wasn't terrible.<br /><br />There are some issues with the book and I'll get them out of the way quickly. First, Matthew Reilly loves italics. I got the distinct impression he read his first draft and decided there just weren't enough slanty letters, so dropped italic dust all over each page, oftentimes on words that don't even need emphasis.<br /><br />He also has a thing for exclamation marks. I'm honestly not used to seeing these outside of speech. If something dramatic happens in a book I assume I'll notice, I don't really need an exclamation mark to tell me.<br /><br />Another punctuation mark of choice is the ellipsis. Far too many times something dramatic started happeneing…<br />… and then was resolved on the next line. If this were a tv series and those dots represented seven days between broadcasts then they would invoke a lot of tension, but when they involve dropping my eyes to the next line, something they have to do every dozen words anyway, all it does is irk.<br /><br />The three issues above are infused in a sentence of comedic genius about half way into the book. I present my favourite sentence in <i>Seven Ancient Wonders</i>:<br /><br />They were being attacked…<br />…<i>from the golf course!</i><br /><br />A perhaps misplaced issue I had with the book is the presence of schematic diagrams of the various places visited in the text. They kind of give the impression that the author doesn't quite trust in his ability to describe the current location, or the reader's ability to imagine it.<br /><br />Finally, and most anally, there's a lot of Egyptian writing mentioned in the book. At their first appearance Reilly called the symbols hieroglyphs, and I rejoiced. Then the next time he said hieroglyphics, and I died a little. He couldn't seem to figure out which one he should use so did what I used to do on French exams and used them both alternately, figuring he'd get at least half of them right. On a similarly pedantic note, at one point he describes a cross shaped room as being "cross shaped", then later describes an identically shaped room as being "†-shaped". Why?<br /><br />Despite all that the book zips along at such a pace that by the time any of these things annoyed me it was already a few pages passed. It's sillier than <i>Da Vinci Code</i> but, as the author says in an interview at the end of the book, the book is more Indiana Jones than Robert Langdon. Which I'd guessed the nineteenth time the heroes triggered a trap that sent a massive boulder chasing them down a slope…<br />… and then they dived out of <i>the way</i> just in time!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1490413472493471419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41517865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17975110680144614491">What do you suppose would happen if an adventure novel got viciously mugged by a big fish tale? Probably something a lot like this. Now listen, if you want paeans to technology, stick to Clancy. Odes to science? Crichton's your man (Miss you already, Michael). But for sheer exuberance, not to mention all the momentum of a monster avalanche, Matthew Reilly is definitely your go-to guy. He's not afraid to use mutant walruses, mutant jaguars, hell, mutant children. <br/>But there are rules here: throw l</span>
  <span id="freeText17975110680144614491" style="display:none">What do you suppose would happen if an adventure novel got viciously mugged by a big fish tale? Probably something a lot like this. Now listen, if you want paeans to technology, stick to Clancy. Odes to science? Crichton's your man (Miss you already, Michael). But for sheer exuberance, not to mention all the momentum of a monster avalanche, Matthew Reilly is definitely your go-to guy. He's not afraid to use mutant walruses, mutant jaguars, hell, mutant children. <br />But there are rules here: throw logic out the window, along with anything you may know about military training, basic psychology, or the physical laws of our local universe. None of that truly matters because what we have here is a smorgasborg of myth, conspiracy theory(my favorite), and Indiana Jones-style schlepping- think Temple of Doom, not Raiders- a confusion of kidnappings, sneakthievery, deaths, almost deaths, etc, etc. In short, possibly the tastiest, most addictive junk food you may ever be privileged to eat. Buy it quick before someone figures out the red dye could kill you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17975110680144614491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_81298043" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81298043" />
    <a title="Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly"><img alt="Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1285872916p2/2276205.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81298043?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly" href="/user/show/2276205-kelly">Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81298043" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14908458282736457303">Some time ago, I gave this book to a friend as a gift. Said friend is a big fan of the archaeological-mystery genre, and this looked to be right up her alley. Then, last weekend, I visited her home and found myself with a few hours to kill. I picked this up and started reading. <br/><br/>I owe my friend an apology. <br/><br/>Wow, what dreck. Or should I say, Wow! What dreck! The author's ridiculously breathless writing style, obviously intended to tell us that This! Story! Is supposed to be! Exciting! in case it sl</span>
  <span id="freeText14908458282736457303" style="display:none">Some time ago, I gave this book to a friend as a gift. Said friend is a big fan of the archaeological-mystery genre, and this looked to be right up her alley. Then, last weekend, I visited her home and found myself with a few hours to kill. I picked this up and started reading. <br /><br />I owe my friend an apology. <br /><br />Wow, what dreck. Or should I say, Wow! What dreck! The author's ridiculously breathless writing style, obviously intended to tell us that This! Story! Is supposed to be! Exciting! in case it slipped our minds, is rivaled only by the implausibility of the plot. The characters go around nearly-dying in nasty traps, complete with choppy exclamatory prose, only to breeze through other traps whenever the author wants to take the easy way out. The thing that finally made me shout audibly at the book was when a torch was falling toward a pool of oil, about to flambe the hero, and his freaking BIRD swooped in and carried the torch away. Unless the bird, whose name is Horus, is ACTUALLY THE GOD HORUS, I don't think so! Good grief. <br /><br />I didn't make it much further than that. So, I must confess, I only followed Gary Stu--I mean Jack--to the first of the seven wonders. I don't think I can take six more wonders' worth of exclamation marks.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14908458282736457303" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1490572181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1490572181" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1490572181?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/28503834-7-deadly-wonders">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rob by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5999881-geoff">Geoff</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=audio-book">audio-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1490572181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9460227843715165651"><b>Executive Summary:</b> This book is ridiculous. I'm torn between a 2 and 3 star rating because it's a solid 2.5. I have to round down because what started off pretty fun got so over the top by the end that I was constantly rolling my eyes.<br/><br/><b>Audiobook:</b> William Dufris is a pretty good narrator that I've enjoyed from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4763.John_Scalzi' title='John Scalzi' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Scalzi</a>'s Old Man War series. He does some voices and is easy to listen to. However, I kept waiting for the characters to start using their Brain Pals. It was a bit hard to separate Mr. </span>
  <span id="freeText9460227843715165651" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> This book is ridiculous. I'm torn between a 2 and 3 star rating because it's a solid 2.5. I have to round down because what started off pretty fun got so over the top by the end that I was constantly rolling my eyes.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook:</b> William Dufris is a pretty good narrator that I've enjoyed from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4763.John_Scalzi" title="John Scalzi" rel="nofollow noopener">John Scalzi</a>'s Old Man War series. He does some voices and is easy to listen to. However, I kept waiting for the characters to start using their Brain Pals. It was a bit hard to separate Mr. Dufris from that series as I listened.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />As 2015 came to a close, I realized just how much fantasy I read last year. Now that's not unusual for me but I used to read a lot more mysteries and thrillers and didn't really get too heavy into fantasy until college.<br /><br />I solicited some recommendations for non-SFF books to check out with the main criteria being light and fun. Apparently I picked the most ridiculous book to start with first. For me the main attraction was the Indiana Jones vibe/the mentions of Ancient Egypt. I loved Ancient Egypt as a kid. One of the main reasons I got in Stargate was its basis in Ancient Egypt.<br /><br />This book is fun, don't get me wrong. However the writing was pretty bad. I also had believability issues. Not only in the "military" actions of some of the characters, but the politics. I get America is not everyone's favorite country. It's totally understandable. Still I have a really hard time believing that Canada, New Zealand, Australia, and Ireland (not the UK) will team up with Spain and the United Arab Emirates against the US. First off that seems a bit random. Second it shows a lack of understanding on the author's part about the nature of the relationship between the major English speaking nations.<br /><br />Even that aside, I have a really hard time believing any nation, will just casually use soldiers as expendable test subjects for ancient traps. It just seemed silly. It wasn't just the Americans either. There was also the evil Europeans made up of France, Germany and the Vatican. What!? I know this is fiction, but seriously..did this guy not learn any world history growing up? I feel like he made his factions by using darts on a map or something.<br /><br />Anyways in addition to the bad writing/unbelievable parts, most of the characters felt paper-thin and cartoonish. By the end I just wanted to be done. It's probably why after long thought I'm rounding my rating down.<br /><br />That said, I did enjoy good chunks of this book. I liked the general premise of the plot, the exploration of ancient tombs/wonders and the various traps they encountered and had to overcome. I bet a better author could have made a really good story out of it.<br /><br />It's too bad because I had pretty high hopes for this one, and since it's book 1 in a series, I figured I'd have a few to read. I just can't though. This author just apparently isn't for me. Still I'm glad I read the book. It's definitely the type of book I was looking to read. Hopefully the next non-SFF pick will go a little better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9460227843715165651" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer549095129283693231">I really enjoyed this book - so much so that I finished it in about a day and a half. I haven't read a book that was so fast paced in a while, the characters were engaging and the storyline was really interesting. I also thought that the illustrations were a good idea, helping to imagine the places described and adding to the story.<br/><br/>The only problem I had with the book was the author's extensive use of italics for emphasis. It fitted well in some instances, but for me it was over-used, becoming d</span>
  <span id="freeText549095129283693231" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this book - so much so that I finished it in about a day and a half. I haven't read a book that was so fast paced in a while, the characters were engaging and the storyline was really interesting. I also thought that the illustrations were a good idea, helping to imagine the places described and adding to the story.<br /><br />The only problem I had with the book was the author's extensive use of italics for emphasis. It fitted well in some instances, but for me it was over-used, becoming distracting and even a little annoying. It seems a little patronising to the reader to italicise a sentence whenever a dangerous trap was triggered or something unusual happened, which was quite a lot.<br /><br />However, overall I REALLY enjoyed it! I'm not usually one to re-read books, but I'll definitely be going back to this one.</span>

<div id="review_2037721865" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2037721865" />
    <a title="Michael Chrobak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33791289-michael-chrobak"><img alt="Michael Chrobak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1479237284p2/33791289.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2037721865?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Chrobak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Chrobak" href="/user/show/33791289-michael-chrobak">Michael Chrobak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2037721865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1366575726301881052">First of all, I didn't finish the book. I simply couldn't. It started off on a positive note, like a lot of first dates I've been on. Unfortunately it ended with a fake phone call, sudden emergency, gotta run - it's not you it's me kind of ending. I'm actually surprised I made it to page 70. <br/><br/>I read this book because the author was recommended to me by a friend. Unfortunately the public library (which is also the high school library in my town) only had three of the authors books - none of which </span>
  <span id="freeText1366575726301881052" style="display:none">First of all, I didn't finish the book. I simply couldn't. It started off on a positive note, like a lot of first dates I've been on. Unfortunately it ended with a fake phone call, sudden emergency, gotta run - it's not you it's me kind of ending. I'm actually surprised I made it to page 70. <br /><br />I read this book because the author was recommended to me by a friend. Unfortunately the public library (which is also the high school library in my town) only had three of the authors books - none of which were ones my friend recommended. Still, I thought, heck - if the author wrote a couple other really good books, then this one is probably good too. Oops...wrong!<br /><br />First, let's look at the writing style, which is choppy and fragmented and appears to be something the author had started when he was in 5th grade, and it sat in a drawer for a few years. Perhaps under duress from his publisher to push out another book that year, he just wrote a few final chapters to this 'masterpiece', when what it really needed was a complete rewrite - or to be re-filed in the round, grey circular bin under the desk. <br /><br />Next, let's look at the genre. This is not High Fantasy, it's more of a Seal Team 6 meets Professor Landon meets Indiana Jones type novel set on this little planet called Earth - where unfortunately we understand and know the way physical objects are supposed to respond within the known dynamics of our universe. Had the author inserted two words early in the first chapter - Alternate Dimension - I would have overlooked the completely unbelievable way things (and people) behave.<br /><br />I do want to honor my friends recommendation, so I will take another trip to the Little Library the Could and ask the frail, diminutive woman behind the counter if they can perhaps order a copy of the two books that were recommended. I can only pray they are better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1366575726301881052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I look forward to reading many more.<br/><br/>This is an action packed adventure tale that doesn't slow down. With rough and tough soldiers and a 10 year old girl that has them all wrapped around her little finger - she changes their call-signs from the tough-guy names to cute, childlike names (Pooh Bear, Stretch, Big Ears) - and still this doesn't make the story any less of</span>
  <span id="freeText16606874471258569299" style="display:none">What can I say - I am officially a die-hard Matt Reilly fan! This was my second book by Reilly and it was as great as the first one! I look forward to reading many more.<br /><br />This is an action packed adventure tale that doesn't slow down. With rough and tough soldiers and a 10 year old girl that has them all wrapped around her little finger - she changes their call-signs from the tough-guy names to cute, childlike names (Pooh Bear, Stretch, Big Ears) - and still this doesn't make the story any less of a thriller. It actually makes the team seem more like a wierd family and makes you care even more about the character. At least that was the case for me!<br /><br />It's a great story, with an Indiana Jones type flair and maybe a bit of Tomb Raider and a touch of James Bond action/inventions..... Is it realistic or turn to history probably not, but it's fiction! Was Indiana Jones believable, nope!, but I still love him and his adventures! :-)</span>
