<div id="review_300118144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300118144" />
    <a title="Tony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6880940-tony"><img alt="Tony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422050910p2/6880940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/300118144?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tony" href="/user/show/6880940-tony">Tony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6880940-tony?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300118144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2430605115210945914">The most fun I had with this book was finding the disconnects and there are plenty to keep you going "huh? what?"<br/><br/>Here's a few for you:<br/><br/>West and his team are looking for a 2500 year old underground entrance. His buddy, carrying the ancient scroll which reveals the secret entrance, consults the scroll and discovers the entrance is marked by 4 lotus trees. And wouldn't ya know, there are the trees! 2500 years later, and still standing!<br/><br/>Pooh Bear gets trapped behind a sliding boulder with no way out e</span>
  <span id="freeText2430605115210945914" style="display:none">The most fun I had with this book was finding the disconnects and there are plenty to keep you going "huh? what?"<br /><br />Here's a few for you:<br /><br />West and his team are looking for a 2500 year old underground entrance. His buddy, carrying the ancient scroll which reveals the secret entrance, consults the scroll and discovers the entrance is marked by 4 lotus trees. And wouldn't ya know, there are the trees! 2500 years later, and still standing!<br /><br />Pooh Bear gets trapped behind a sliding boulder with no way out except to jump into a spiked pit or another pit so deep there is no way out. But he manages to show up later.<br /><br />Near the end, West throws a punch at a bad guy with his metal fist: "the best punch he'd ever thrown with his all-metal left hand-<br />The blow connected...and had no effect on Kallis at all."<br />A few seconds later West throws another punch at Kallis with the same hand and this punch caves his nose into his face 3 inches, a soon to be fatal blow. But the best punch he ever connected with had no effect. Ya, this was a "huh? what?" moment for me.<br /><br />There was too many unnecessary F-bombs and motherF-bombs in the book. I don't recall Indiana Jones using language like that. It adds nothing to the story and only tells me the author is looking to find some kind of shock value in language where he couldn't add it by the story itself.<br /><br />Reilly even takes a poke at George Bush by calling him an imperialist in the questions section at the back. This seemed to be a popular pass-time back in 2006 but I don't care much for it so that cost Reilly another star rating. Isn't imperialism when a country tries to expand its authority over other countries? Like England over (ahem) Australia. Not a good idea to use your fiction books as a platform for your politics, Matt, old buddy. It could blow up in your face.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2430605115210945914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer959244882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10466233304199265927">I'm a huge fan of Matthew Reilly's books. Even with it's total lack of characterization and plot, it's insane over-abundance of exclamation points!!!, and the fact that it reads like something that came from the mind of a sugar-fed fourth grader with ADHD, Ice Station is still one of my very favorite books of all time. It was fun! And exciting!, and in a weird way, the fact that it was written rather poorly, kind of fit it , and added to the overall reading experience. This book, however, was a </span>
  <span id="freeText10466233304199265927" style="display:none">I'm a huge fan of Matthew Reilly's books. Even with it's total lack of characterization and plot, it's insane over-abundance of exclamation points!!!, and the fact that it reads like something that came from the mind of a sugar-fed fourth grader with ADHD, Ice Station is still one of my very favorite books of all time. It was fun! And exciting!, and in a weird way, the fact that it was written rather poorly, kind of fit it , and added to the overall reading experience. This book, however, was a piece of crap. I think. I never got past the first 50 pages. Horribly, horribly written, and not in a good way. Unlike Ice Station, this book had a plot, but it sucked. It made a play at characterization, but the characters sucked. The overblown action scenes in Reilly's other books, which were long and ridiculous, and unbelievable (but fun!), were way too overblown in this one, and just ended up being stupid nonsense. I love Reilly's stuff, but this book sucked ass. But not in a good, "hey baby, we're gonna try something different tonight. I wanna toss your salad" way. Boo on this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10466233304199265927" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer17379086&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer17379086" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15659171007384151306">I loved all of his previous books - well, with exception of Hover Car Racer, which was ok, but not for me, i.e. it was Young Readers and showed. But this was just silly. Lots of action as usual, which I like. But otherwise it felt like reading a comic or playing a first person shooter. The heroes were endlessly going through the same chapter over and over again. Problem of getting through a maze without getting killed by the traps, neat little sketch that gets repeated several times and everythi</span>
  <span id="freeText15659171007384151306" style="display:none">I loved all of his previous books - well, with exception of Hover Car Racer, which was ok, but not for me, i.e. it was Young Readers and showed. But this was just silly. Lots of action as usual, which I like. But otherwise it felt like reading a comic or playing a first person shooter. The heroes were endlessly going through the same chapter over and over again. Problem of getting through a maze without getting killed by the traps, neat little sketch that gets repeated several times and everything neatly pointed out with exclamation marks and highlighted in Italics, so you really do not miss when you are supposed to be excited and dying from the suspense - in case you are too thick to get it by yourself. Was he still writing for 12 year olds? I almost did not finish it, it was so shallow and the plot so simplistic, I couldn't decide if I should feel insulted or just throw it in the bin. Sorry Mr Reilly, you lost me.</span>

    <a title="Janey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56437304-janey"><img alt="Janey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464944264p2/56437304.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1656369564?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Janey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Janey" href="/user/show/56437304-janey">Janey</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1656369564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5992176509160314749">There isn't a Matthew Reilly book that I haven't read yet that I haven't enjoyed.<br/><br/>If you like fast-paced, oh-my-God-I-can't-believe-this-is-happening type of books that are full of the literally unbelievable, then you'll also enjoy this book.<br/><br/>The described locations, such as Giza pyramid was just one of the amazing settings as a massive puzzle must be solved in order for our hero to save the world. <br/><br/>Jack West is one of my favorite characters by Matthew Reilly. </span>

<div id="review_3626940533" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3626940533" />
    <a title="AltLovesBooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7975452-altlovesbooks"><img alt="AltLovesBooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569717483p2/7975452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3626940533?book_show_action=true">Nov 11, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AltLovesBooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AltLovesBooks" href="/user/show/7975452-altlovesbooks">AltLovesBooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7975452-altlovesbooks?shelf=audiobooks-read">audiobooks-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7975452-altlovesbooks?shelf=book-lovers-club">book-lovers-club</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7975452-altlovesbooks?shelf=horror-thriller">horror-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3626940533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3655100427408682492"><i>*SHOOM*</i><br/><br/>I don't read a lot of action thrillers. Most of them read as being really formulaic to me, and I can't seem to turn my brain off enough to just enjoy the ride. This one especially reads like Indiana Jones had a fling with (Inter)National Treasure, and brought their child up like Lara Croft. The team is a ragtag group, each hailing from a different small(? Under-represented? Not the US or EU?) country, each awesome at literally everything. No, seriously, everything. The hero, Jack West, ma</span>
  <span id="freeText3655100427408682492" style="display:none"><i>*SHOOM*</i><br /><br />I don't read a lot of action thrillers. Most of them read as being really formulaic to me, and I can't seem to turn my brain off enough to just enjoy the ride. This one especially reads like Indiana Jones had a fling with (Inter)National Treasure, and brought their child up like Lara Croft. The team is a ragtag group, each hailing from a different small(? Under-represented? Not the US or EU?) country, each awesome at literally everything. No, seriously, everything. The hero, Jack West, manages to be especially awesome at literally everything. Time gets all wibblywobbly as our team of heroes manages to circle the globe in just a few days, but that's okay because everyone manages to be right where they should be at exactly the right moments. <br /><br />I sort of enjoyed the ride, but not because it was action-packed thriller material. I moreso enjoyed it for the camp. The constant comic book noises (BAM! ZOOM! WOOSH! SHOOM!) were especially amusing, and Lily's "SWEAR JAR!" was kind of endearing, actually. But the rest? I dunno, I can't suspend my disbelief enough to accept a lot of what happened. <br /><br />Can we all just agree that Horus is the real star of this?</span>
  <a data-text-id="3655100427408682492" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_258442606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/258442606" />
    <a title="Paulo &quot;paper books always&quot; Carvalho" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3789445-paulo-paper-books-always-carvalho"><img alt="Paulo &quot;paper books always&quot; Carvalho" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465225442p2/3789445.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/258442606?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paulo &quot;paper books always&quot; Carvalho" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paulo &quot;paper books always&quot; Carvalho" href="/user/show/3789445-paulo-paper-books-always-carvalho">Paulo &quot;paper books always&quot; Carvalho</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780330426572" href="/book/show/1282342.Seven_Ancient_Wonders">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789445-paulo-paper-books-always-carvalho?shelf=trying-to-trade">trying-to-trade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789445-paulo-paper-books-always-carvalho?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789445-paulo-paper-books-always-carvalho?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789445-paulo-paper-books-always-carvalho?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3789445-paulo-paper-books-always-carvalho?shelf=series_dropped">series_dropped</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer258442606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer250377638971714113">Ahhh...<br/><br/>Finally it's over. I am undecided on how many stars I am going to give. After making my review I will decide.<br/><br/><br/>So, what have we got here... A <b>action-slash-adventure thriller</b> book sure reads like a movie script.<br/><br/>First of all I nearly gave up after reading 78 pages and after my second, third and each attempt I read but I don't want to leave any unfinish book.<br/><br/>I have so many critics that I don't know how to begin. I know this is FICTION novel but at the same time I know this is not fantasy and n</span>
  <span id="freeText250377638971714113" style="display:none">Ahhh...<br><br>Finally it's over. I am undecided on how many stars I am going to give. After making my review I will decide.<br><br><br>So, what have we got here... A <b>action-slash-adventure thriller</b> book sure reads like a movie script.<br><br>First of all I nearly gave up after reading 78 pages and after my second, third and each attempt I read but I don't want to leave any unfinish book.<br><br>I have so many critics that I don't know how to begin. I know this is FICTION novel but at the same time I know this is not fantasy and neither SF so there are some things that I sure accept as "writer's liberty".<br><br><b>First</b> of all are the characters. The main character is a uber character near invicible. No matter how many times they try to kill him he will escape. No harm can befall him. So I didn't care about him. <br><br><b>Second</b> his partners in adventure are what they are. Muslism are muslims, israelites are what you expect from one of them. And so on.<br><br><b>Third</b> The Enemies. Oh my god! The story goes like this... The europeans task force is something something invicible awesome but then a couple chapters after they die like a vietnamese in a Rambo movie. Then come the americans. They are the best of the best and bang come the vietnamese. Then come the isralites... oh no, they are the best of the best of the best and vietnamese become... They sure look like Stormtroopers in a Stars Wars movies. They are the best of all galaxy but sure don't hit a damn thing in all movies.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380366797i/719135.jpg" width="350" height="290" alt="Always missing" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380366797i/719136.jpg" width="150" height="150" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380366797i/719137.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>In this case change bond's villains to West's villains. It's the same thing.<br><br><b>Four</b> How in the name of Amun-Ra they could make all their travels in under 7 days? How in name of God could they find all those hidden wonders in such short time. You know Iraq is sure big enough and the Tunisian's Coast to cover in just couple of hours.<br><br><br><b>Five</b> If only was that easy to take someone from the Guantanamo bay.<br><br><b>Six</b> Oh my god... the hawk. I want it. I really want it because he is a smart as a person and can fly. <br><br><b>Seven</b> Then you've got all those traps with crocodiles... What the heck do they eat inside a mountain closed for 4 thousand years? Maybe they are cannibals... <br><br>Really man.. I am going to type here this sentence<br><br><i>"He leapt from the walkay onto the stepping-stone -- and immediately heard a rush of water from up inside the wall-hole, accompained by a low crocodilian growl --<br>-at which point he jammed his titanium X-bar into the wall-hole and hit a switchon the bar.<br>Thwack!<br>The x-shaped bar expanded with a powerful springloaded motion, so that suddenly it was wedhed tightly in the mouth of the circular wall-hole.<br>Not a second too soon.<br>An instant later, a burst of water gushed out of the wall-hole, immedately followed by the jaws of a massive crocodile that slammed at tremendous speed into the X-Bar!<br>The croc roared angrily but its jaws were caught against the X-bar unable to get past. The rush of water sprayed all around Fuzzy, but didn't knock him over."</i><br><br>So the water fall followed by a crocodile.... Where was this crocodile? It was there awaiting patiently for 4000 years to the trap sprang? Talk about epic fail... both of the croc and the writer.<br><br>Just to finish. This main character twist the neck of a crocodile. AWESOME!!!<br><br><b>Eight</b> The ending. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ So the Australians are invicible now. Ok, good. So the next two books Jack West is even more amazing than this one right? I like the part when Jack and Wizard talk about not saying anything to the Australians. So Australia will rule. How? Militaristic of economic? What will happen when one australian tries to kill another? Their weapon will fail as Judah did? What?? Sorry. Weak Ending.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Now the positive parts<br><b>One</b> The history bit. All the stories behind it. The connection between the egyptians and the catholic church and the free masons. The connection between nowadays buildings and the ancient wonders. That part I liked. It's another way of seeing things.<br><br><b>Two</b> The americans are evil militaristic nation with the old european nations. The rest of the world must join and battle them. It was another change of setting. Usually the americans are the good guys.<br><br><b>Three</b> All the drawings and pictures inside the book really gave the book another feeling. Sometimes when I am reading a book with a detail information about something I sure would like to see a picture to make it easier. This book help me a lot. I really enjoy that. And For that I will give you a bonus star.<br><br><br>In the end my <b>conclusion</b> is this:<br>You wanna read a fast paced thriller in a plane or a train under 5/6/7 hours? Then I advice it to you. You wanna read a book alike Da Vinci Code, Go for it. Other person read at your own peril.<br><br>I would give one star. But the historic part and the drawings and pictures deserve a second star. Will I read the next one (that I bought after enjoying a lot Contest and thinking it would be similar)? Maybe. If I would want to read a fast paced book but soft on the mind.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="250377638971714113" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CDzFAEdu8V/ic/ueaNcQdkkqNMaNEglHaouhSxEIzaqkPQOdzLXcUuCr1RltNauoRmbG6HDSr/KtCaG9696BOA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z0D+CTtZjzdhoPnBu+OAF/6IQqejBl4WfjeFdzDJRfbLQTiUsIKiOmN410a+ATvJ8cSwiV7G+KO5tYWByh8JZA==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/83714.Matthew_Reilly">About Matthew Reilly</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/83714.Matthew_Reilly"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1309746050p3/83714.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8003654668524843325">Born in Sydney in 1974, Matthew Reilly was not always a big fan of reading. It was only after he read To Kill A Mockingbird and Lord of the Flies in Year 10 that he realised reading could transport you to another world. Following this revelation, Matthew soon began creating stories of his own and set about writing his first novel, Contest, at the age of 19 while still at university studying law.<br/><br/>Fo</span>
  <span id="freeText8003654668524843325" style="display:none">Born in Sydney in 1974, Matthew Reilly was not always a big fan of reading. It was only after he read To Kill A Mockingbird and Lord of the Flies in Year 10 that he realised reading could transport you to another world. Following this revelation, Matthew soon began creating stories of his own and set about writing his first novel, Contest, at the age of 19 while still at university studying law.<br /><br />Following rejections from all the major publishers, Matthew self-published Contest in 1996, printing 1000 copies. He produced a big-budget-looking novel which he sold into bookshops throughout Sydney, one shop at a time.<br /><br />In January 1997, a Commissioning Editor for Pan Macmillan Australia walked into Angus &amp; Robertson's Pitt Street Mall store and bought a copy of Contest. The editor tracked Matthew down through his contact details in the front of the book. Interestingly, those original self-published editions of Contest have now become much sought after collectors' items. One recently sold on eBay for $1200!<br /><br />Matthew Reilly is now the internationally bestselling author of the Scarecrow novels: Ice Station, Area 7, Scarecrow, Scarecrow and the Army of Thieves and the novella Hell Island; the Jack West novels: Seven Ancient Wonders, The Six Sacred Stones, The Five Greatest Warriors, The Four Legendary Kingdoms, and The Three Secret Cities; and the standalone novels Contest, Temple, Hover Car Racer, The Tournament, Troll Mountain, The Great Zoo of China and The Secret Runners of New York.<br /><br />His books are published in over 20 languages with worldwide sales of over 7 million copies.<br /><br />Since Seven Ancient Wonders in 2005, Matthew's novels have been the biggest selling new fiction title released in Australia for that year.<br /><br />Matthew has also written several short stories, including Roger Ascham and the King's Lost Girl, a special free prequel to The Tournament which is available online. Other short stories include Time Tours, The Mine and the hyper-adrenalised romp, Altitude Rush.<br /><br />He owns and drives a DeLorean DMC-12, the car made famous in the Back to the Future movies. He also has a life-sized Han Solo in carbonite hanging on the wall of his office! When not writing or penning a film script, Matthew can be found on the golf course.<br /><br />Matthew Reilly is currently living in Los Angeles.<br /><br />(source: Amazon)</span>
  <a data-text-id="8003654668524843325" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

After their thrilling exploits in Matthew Reilly\'s rampaging New York Times bestseller, 7 Deadly Wonders, supersoldier Jack West Jr. and his loyal team of adventurers are back, and now they face an all-but-impossible challenge.A mysterious ceremony in an unknown location has unraveled their work and triggered a catastrophic countdown that will climax in no less than the end of all life on Earth.But there is one last hope.If Jack and his team can find and rebuild a legendary ancient device known only as the &quot;Machine,&quot; they might be able to ward off the coming armageddon.   if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
